The petitioner contended that the resident associations had refused to comply with the provisions of the PCA Act, which prohibits the owners/residents of individual apartments from keeping their pets therein while keeping them therein. However, the petitioner argued that, in the eyes of the court, the residents have no right to keep their pets in the residential apartments and appurtenant premises while keeping the pets therein, and the same can not be said to be a violation of their fundamental right to privacy under Article 20 of our Constitution. Thus, the petition was dismissed by the court. The respondent

The Supreme Court has held that when a person dies in an accident by falling down from a train, it is not possible for the legal heirs to produce the ticket or valid authority to travel in the train. A bench comprising Justices MR Shah and BV Nagarathna observed thus while dismissing a claim filed by the father of the deceased who died in an untoward incident. The court held that death or injury in the course of boarding or deboarding a train will be an'untoward event'entitling a victim to the compensation. `` The concept of'self inflicted injury'would require intention to inflict such injury and not mere negligence of any particular degree, " the bench said. The Court was dealing with an appeal filed by a woman who had filed a Claim Application on account of death of her father namely Shri Suraj Ganvir. She claimed that her father was not a bona fide passenger as no ticket was found with him and therefore, the claimant had made false claim and railway is not responsible for the incident. In her appeal, the High Court held that the deceased was a'bonafide passenger'and thus, she was not entitled to compensation. The case in brief Essentially, the appellant/victim had filed an appeal on the ground of death

The Supreme Court has observed that an employer can not interfere with the proceedings of a departmental enquiry and trial of a criminal case. In this case, the respondent's service came to be dismissed from service by order dated 2nd March, 2021. A Division Bench of Justices MR Shah and BV Nagarathna observed that the order of dismissal of the respondent can not be sustained. The bench was dealing with a writ petition filed by the respondent challenging the dismissal order passed by the Division Bench. The respondent, who was a Depot Manager, A.P. SRTC v. Mohd. Yousuf 548, AIR 1997 SC 2232, was dismissed on the ground that he had already revealed his defence by participating in the proceedings. As per the order, he was dismissed from the service on the grounds that he was not cooperating with the enquiry. It was further held that there is no bar to proceed simultaneously with the criminal enquiry, trial of the criminal case, and the final order of penalty would not debar an employer from exercising the power to conduct departmental proceedings. However, the bench noted that the orders of dismissal were not applicable to the criminal proceedings.

The Supreme Court has observed that a law can not be struck down merely because a better policy/course of action could be adopted. The bench comprising Justices MR Shah and BV Nagarathna observed thus while hearing a plea challenging the validity of Clause 2 ( c ) of the Rajasthan State Road Transport Corporation Compassionate Appointment of the Dependents of Deceased Employees Regulations, 2022. The Bench was hearing the plea filed by two petitioners, who were married and had adopted a daughter, for whom, there is no such restriction or qua an unmarried daughter itself. The petitioners were married, they could not be debarred from consideration for grant of compassionate appointment as they otherwise fulfill all the requisite considerations. The court was hearing an appeal filed by the petitioners challenging the decision of the State Government to grant compassionate appointment to their daughter, who was legally adopted by a deceased Government servant during his/her life time. The Petitioners contended that the provision restricting the definition to 'unmarried'before daughter in the provision, by itself is discriminatory and violative of Articles 14 to 16 of the Constitution of India. The High Court held that the policy of compassionate appointments is to assuage the immediate financial hardship of the incumbent Government servant.
